\doxysubsection{Detailed Description}
{\bfseries{ M\+QC Algebra contains mathematical objects that are designed to simplify and automate variable use in Fortran }} 

\begin{DoxyParagraph}{Purpose\+:}
\begin{DoxyVerb}    MQC Algebra contains mathematical objects that are designed to simplify
    and automate variable use in Fortran. Arrays can be packed for efficient 
    memory use and used for operations completely transparently to the user. 
    Furthermore, there is no need to type arrays, as this can be manipulated 
    on the fly. Arrays carry their own procedures, and use underlying lapack 
    routines for efficiency. The MQC derivd types defined in this package 
    are:

    1. MQC_Scalar:   Rank 0 array variable
    2. MQC_Vector:   Rank 1 array variable
    3. MQC_Matrix:   Rank 2 array variable
    4. MQC_R4Tensor: Rank 3 array variable

    This module is level 1 in the MQC hierarchy and so depends on level 0
    modules. 

    Note that MQC_Algebra2 provides similar functionality with MQC_Array 
    objects that can dynamically adjust rank. However, the vast majority of 
    work can be performed using MQC_Algebra derived types which have been 
    more developed than MQC_Algebra2 derived types.\end{DoxyVerb}
 
\end{DoxyParagraph}

{\bfseries{ Bin\+\_\+\+Coeff returns the binomial coefficient of (n,k)}} 

\begin{DoxyParagraph}{Purpose\+:}
\begin{DoxyVerb}    Bin_Coeff is a function that returns the binomial coefficient given input
    integer N and input integer K corresponding to N choose K.\end{DoxyVerb}
 
\end{DoxyParagraph}

{\footnotesize\ttfamily subroutine mqc\+\_\+algebra\+::mqc\+\_\+allocate\+\_\+matrix (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{integer(kind=int64), intent(in)}]{M,  }\item[{integer(kind=int64), intent(in)}]{N,  }\item[{class(\mbox{\hyperlink{structmqc__algebra_1_1mqc__matrix}{mqc\+\_\+matrix}}), intent(inout)}]{Matrix,  }\item[{character(len=$\ast$), intent(in)}]{Data\+\_\+\+Type,  }\item[{character(len=$\ast$), intent(in)}]{Storage }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}



{\bfseries{ M\+Q\+C\+\_\+\+Allocate\+\_\+\+Matrix is used to allocate a matrix type variable of the M\+Q\+C\+\_\+\+Matrix class}} 

\begin{DoxyParagraph}{Purpose\+:}
\begin{DoxyVerb}    MQC_Allocate_Matrix is a subroutine used to allocate a matrix type variable
    of the MQC_Matrix class. The following options are available:

    1. Data_Type = 'Real' declares the MQC_Matrix variable to be of real type. 
    2. Data_Type = 'Integer' declares the MQC_Matrix variable to be of integer type.
    3. Data_Type = 'Complex' declares the MQC_Matrix variable to be of complex type.
    4. Storage = 'StorFull' declares the MQC_Matrix variable to be unpacked.
    5. Storage = 'StorSymm' declares the MQC_Matrix variable to be symmetric packed.
    6. Storage = 'StorDiag' declares the MQC_Matrix variable to be diagonal packed.\end{DoxyVerb}
 
\end{DoxyParagraph}

\begin{DoxyParams}[1]{Parameters}
\mbox{\texttt{ in}}  & {\em M} & \begin{DoxyVerb}        M is Integer(kind=int64)
        M is the number of rows of Matrix. \end{DoxyVerb}
\\
\hline
\mbox{\texttt{ in}}  & {\em N} & \begin{DoxyVerb}        N is Integer(kind=int64)
        N is the number of columns of Matrix.\end{DoxyVerb}
\\
\hline
\mbox{\texttt{ in,out}}  & {\em Matrix} & \begin{DoxyVerb}        Matrix is Class(MQC_Matrix)
        The MQC matrix to be allocated.\end{DoxyVerb}
\\
\hline
\mbox{\texttt{ in}}  & {\em Data\+\_\+\+Type} & \begin{DoxyVerb}        Data_Type is Character(Len=*)
        = 'Real':    the MQC_Matrix is real
        = 'Integer': the MQC_Matrix is integer
        = 'Complex': the MQC_Matrix is complex.\end{DoxyVerb}
\\
\hline
\mbox{\texttt{ in}}  & {\em Storage} & ~\newline
 \begin{DoxyVerb}        Storage is Character(Len=*)
        = 'StorFull': the MQC_Matrix is unpacked
        = 'StorSymm': the MQC_Matrix is symmetric packed
        = 'StorDiag': the MQC_Matrix is diagonal packed.\end{DoxyVerb}
 \\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}
\begin{DoxyAuthor}{Author}
H. P. Hratchian 

L. M. Thompson 
\end{DoxyAuthor}
\begin{DoxyDate}{Date}
2016 
\end{DoxyDate}

{\footnotesize\ttfamily logical function mqc\+\_\+algebra\+::mqc\+\_\+integergtscalar (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{integer(kind=int64), intent(in)}]{Int\+In,  }\item[{type(\mbox{\hyperlink{structmqc__algebra_1_1mqc__scalar}{mqc\+\_\+scalar}}), intent(in)}]{Scalar }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}



{\bfseries{ M\+Q\+C\+\_\+\+Integer\+G\+T\+Scalar is a function that returns T\+R\+UE if an intrinsic integer is greater than a M\+Q\+C\+\_\+\+Scalar}} 

\begin{DoxyParagraph}{Purpose\+:}
\begin{DoxyVerb}    MQC_IntegerGTScalar is a function that returns TRUE if an intrinsic integer is greater 
    than a MQC_Scalar. 

    When dealing with complex numbers, the function returns TRUE if the intrinsic integer 
    is greater than the real part of the MQC_Scalar and FALSE if the intrinsic integer is 
    less than the real part of the MQC_Scalar. If the intrinsic integer is equal to the
    real part of the MQC_Scalar, the function returns TRUE if the imaginary part of 
    MQC_Scalar is less than zero and FALSE otherwise. \end{DoxyVerb}
 
\end{DoxyParagraph}

\begin{DoxyParams}[1]{Parameters}
\mbox{\texttt{ in}}  & {\em Int\+In} & \begin{DoxyVerb}        IntIn is Integer(kind=int64)
        The intrinsic integer that will be tested.\end{DoxyVerb}
\\
\hline
\mbox{\texttt{ in}}  & {\em Scalar} & \begin{DoxyVerb}        Scalar is Type(MQC_Scalar)
        The MQC_Scalar that will be tested.\end{DoxyVerb}
 \\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}
\begin{DoxyAuthor}{Author}
L. M. Thompson 
\end{DoxyAuthor}
\begin{DoxyDate}{Date}
2019 
\end{DoxyDate}

{\bfseries{ M\+Q\+C\+\_\+\+Integer\+L\+E\+Scalar is a function that returns T\+R\+UE if an intrinsic integer is less than or equal to a M\+Q\+C\+\_\+\+Scalar}} 

\begin{DoxyParagraph}{Purpose\+:}
\begin{DoxyVerb}    MQC_IntegerLEScalar is a function that returns TRUE if an intrinsic integer is less 
    than or equal to a MQC_Scalar. 

    When dealing with complex numbers, the function returns TRUE if the intrinsic integer 
    is less than or equal to the real part of the MQC_Scalar and FALSE if the intrinsic 
    integer is greater than the real part of the MQC_Scalar.\end{DoxyVerb}

    determines the initial packing of MQC matrix.\end{DoxyVerb}

{\bfseries{ M\+Q\+C\+\_\+\+Matrix\+\_\+\+Matrix\+\_\+\+At is a function that returns a submatrix of the matrix}} 

\begin{DoxyParagraph}{Purpose\+:}
\begin{DoxyVerb}    MQC_Matrix_Matrix_At is a function that returns the matrix between rows (I,J) and 
    columns (K,L) of an MQC_Matrix Mat as an MQC_Matrix Matrix. If I, J, K or L is 
    negative, the (N-I+1)th index value is selected.\end{DoxyVerb}
 
\end{DoxyParagraph}

\begin{DoxyParams}[1]{Parameters}
\mbox{\texttt{ in}}  & {\em Mat} & \begin{DoxyVerb}        Mat is Class(MQC_Matrix)
        Name of the input matrix variable\end{DoxyVerb}
\\
\hline
\mbox{\texttt{ in}}  & {\em rows} & \begin{DoxyVerb}        Rows is Integer(kind=int64),Dimension(:)
        If = [A,B]: output is submatrix of rows A to B
          If (A,B)>0 row count is from first index
          If (A,B)<0 row count is from last index
        If = [0]: submatrix of rows equivalent to [1,-1].\end{DoxyVerb}
\\
\hline
\mbox{\texttt{ in}}  & {\em Cols} & \begin{DoxyVerb}        Cols is Integer(kind=int64),Dimension(:)
        If = [A,B]: output is submatrix of columns A to B
          If (A,B)>0 column count is from first index
          If (A,B)<0 column count is from last index
        If = [0]: submatrix of columns equivalent to [1,-1].\end{DoxyVerb}
 \\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}

{\footnotesize\ttfamily recursive subroutine mqc\+\_\+algebra\+::mqc\+\_\+matrix\+\_\+matrix\+\_\+put (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{class(\mbox{\hyperlink{structmqc__algebra_1_1mqc__matrix}{mqc\+\_\+matrix}}), intent(inout)}]{Mat,  }\item[{type(\mbox{\hyperlink{structmqc__algebra_1_1mqc__matrix}{mqc\+\_\+matrix}}), intent(in)}]{Matrix\+In,  }\item[{integer(kind=int64), dimension(\+:), intent(in)}]{Rows,  }\item[{integer(kind=int64), dimension(\+:), intent(in)}]{Cols }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}



{\bfseries{ M\+Q\+C\+\_\+\+Matrix\+\_\+\+Matrix\+\_\+\+Put is a subroutine that writes a submatrix to the specified position of a M\+QC matrix}} 

\begin{DoxyParagraph}{Purpose\+:}
\begin{DoxyVerb}    MQC_Matrix_Matrix_Put is a subroutine that writes a submatrix to the specified
    position of a MQC matrix. The row and column specification are given as a vector 
    where each vector must contain either zero or two non-zero integers to specify 
    the range of elements that will be overwritten by the submatrix. If the value 
    of an element specification is negative, it counts from the last element back. 
    If the value of an element specification is zero, the whole row/column is 
    specified.\end{DoxyVerb}
 
\end{DoxyParagraph}

\begin{DoxyParams}[1]{Parameters}
\mbox{\texttt{ in,out}}  & {\em Mat} & \begin{DoxyVerb}        Mat is Class(MQC_Matrix)
        The MQC matrix from which to return the subvector.\end{DoxyVerb}
\\
\hline
\mbox{\texttt{ in}}  & {\em Matrix\+In} & \begin{DoxyVerb}        MatrixIn is Type(MQC_Matrix)
        The submatrix to overwrite at the specified elements 
        of Mat.\end{DoxyVerb}
\\
\hline
\mbox{\texttt{ in}}  & {\em Rows} & \begin{DoxyVerb}        Rows is Integer(kind=int64),Dimension(:)
        The specification of the rows to include in the 
        subvector. 
        If = [A,B]: output is subvector of rows A to B
          If (A,B)>0 row count is from first index
          If (A,B)<0 row count is from last index
        If = [0]: subvector of rows equivalent to [1,-1].\end{DoxyVerb}
\\
\hline
\mbox{\texttt{ in}}  & {\em Cols} & ~\newline
 \begin{DoxyVerb}        Cols is Integer(kind=int64),Dimension(:)
        The specification of the columns to include in the 
        subvector. 
        If = [A,B]: output is subvector of columns A to B
          If (A,B)>0 column count is from first index
          If (A,B)<0 column count is from last index
        If = [0]: subvector of columns equivalent to [1,-1].\end{DoxyVerb}
 \\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}

{\footnotesize\ttfamily type(\mbox{\hyperlink{structmqc__algebra_1_1mqc__scalar}{mqc\+\_\+scalar}}) function mqc\+\_\+algebra\+::mqc\+\_\+matrix\+\_\+norm (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{class(\mbox{\hyperlink{structmqc__algebra_1_1mqc__matrix}{mqc\+\_\+matrix}}), intent(inout)}]{matrix,  }\item[{character(len=1), intent(in), optional}]{method\+In }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}



{\bfseries{ M\+Q\+C\+\_\+\+Matrix\+\_\+\+Norm is a function that returns the norm of an M\+QC matrix}} 

\begin{DoxyParagraph}{Purpose\+:}
\begin{DoxyVerb}    MQC_Matrix_Norm is a function that returns the norm of an MQC matrix. The 
    following options are available:

    1. methodIn = 'M' uses the maximum absolute value max(abs(A(i,j))).
    2. methodIn = '1' uses the one norm.
    3. methodIn = 'I' uses the infinity norm.
    4. methodIn = 'F' uses the Frobenius norm (default).\end{DoxyVerb}
 
\end{DoxyParagraph}

\begin{DoxyParams}[1]{Parameters}
\mbox{\texttt{ in,out}}  & {\em Matrix} & \begin{DoxyVerb}        Matrix is Class(MQC_Matrix)
        The name of the MQC_Matrix variable.\end{DoxyVerb}
\\
\hline
\mbox{\texttt{ in}}  & {\em Method\+In} & \begin{DoxyVerb}        MethodIn is Character(len=1)
        = 'M': max(abs(A(i,j)))
        = '1': one norm
        = 'I': infinity norm
        = 'F': Frobenius norm.\end{DoxyVerb}
 \\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}
\begin{DoxyAuthor}{Author}
L. M. Thompson 
\end{DoxyAuthor}
\begin{DoxyDate}{Date}
2017 
\end{DoxyDate}

{\bfseries{ M\+Q\+C\+\_\+\+Matrix\+\_\+\+Set is a subroutine that sets an M\+QC matrix to a value without resizing its dimensions}} 

\begin{DoxyParagraph}{Purpose\+:}
\begin{DoxyVerb}    MQC_Matrix_Set is a subroutine that sets an MQC matrix to a value without
    resizing its dimensions. Optional argument scalar specifies the value to set
    each element of the matrix, where the default value is 0.0. Optional argument
    storage allows the storage of the matrix to be defined, where the default is
    unpacked. \end{DoxyVerb}
 
\end{DoxyParagraph}

{\footnotesize\ttfamily subroutine mqc\+\_\+algebra\+::mqc\+\_\+matrix\+\_\+symm2full (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{type(\mbox{\hyperlink{structmqc__algebra_1_1mqc__matrix}{mqc\+\_\+matrix}}), intent(inout)}]{Matrix,  }\item[{character(len=$\ast$), intent(in), optional}]{Option }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}



{\bfseries{ M\+Q\+C\+\_\+\+Matrix\+\_\+\+Symm2\+Full is a subroutine that converts a symmetry-\/packed M\+QC matrix to unpacked}} 

\begin{DoxyParagraph}{Purpose\+:}
\begin{DoxyVerb}    MQC_Matrix_Symm2Full is a subroutine that converts a symmetry-packed MQC matrix 
    to unpacked. The following options are available:
      Option = 'symmetric' unpacks as if matrix is symmetric.
      Option = 'antisymmetric' unpacks as if matrix is antisymmetric.
      Option = 'hermitian' unpacks as if matrix is hermitian.
      Option = 'antihermitian' unpacks as if matrix is antihermitian.

      TODO: when different symm storage flags implemented, use these rather than an
            option\end{DoxyVerb}
 
\end{DoxyParagraph}

\begin{DoxyParams}[1]{Parameters}
\mbox{\texttt{ in,out}}  & {\em Matrix} & \begin{DoxyVerb}        Matrix is Type(MQC_Matrix)
        The MQC matrix to unpack.\end{DoxyVerb}
\\
\hline
\mbox{\texttt{ in}}  & {\em Option} & \begin{DoxyVerb}        Option is Character(len=*),Optional
        = 'symmetric':      Unpack as if matrix is symmetric
        = 'antisymmetric':  Unpack as if matrix is antisymmetric
        = 'hermitian':      Unpack as if matrix is hermitian
        = 'antihermitian':  Unpack as if matrix is antihermitian\end{DoxyVerb}
 \\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}

\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{mqc\_matrix\_test\_symmetric()}{mqc\_matrix\_test\_symmetric()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily logical function mqc\+\_\+algebra\+::mqc\+\_\+matrix\+\_\+test\+\_\+symmetric (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{class(\mbox{\hyperlink{structmqc__algebra_1_1mqc__matrix}{mqc\+\_\+matrix}}), intent(in)}]{Matrix,  }\item[{character(len=$\ast$), intent(in), optional}]{Option }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}



{\bfseries{ M\+Q\+C\+\_\+\+Matrix\+\_\+\+Test\+\_\+\+Symmetric is a function that tests a M\+QC matrix for symmetry}} 

\begin{DoxyParagraph}{Purpose\+:}
\begin{DoxyVerb}    MQC_Matrix_Test_Symmetric is a function that tests a MQC matrix for symmetry 
    specified by optional argument, with the default test being for a symmetric
    matrix. Note that this function differs from haveSymmetric subroutine which
    tests how a matrix is packed. The following options are available: 

    1. Option = 'symmetric' tests for a symmetric matrix (default).
    2. Option = 'antisymmetric' tests for an antisymmetric matrix.
    3. Option = 'hermitian' tests for a hermitian matrix.
    4. Option = 'antihermitian' tests for an antihermitian matrix.\end{DoxyVerb}
 
\end{DoxyParagraph}

\begin{DoxyParams}[1]{Parameters}
\mbox{\texttt{ in}}  & {\em Matrix} & \begin{DoxyVerb}        Matrix is Class(mqc_matrix)
        The matrix to be tested for symmetry.\end{DoxyVerb}
\\
\hline
\mbox{\texttt{ in}}  & {\em Option} & \begin{DoxyVerb}        Option is Character(len=*),Optional
        = 'symmetric':     symmetric matrix test
        = 'antisymmetric': antisymmetric matrix test
        = 'hermitian':     hermitian matrix test
        = 'antihermitian': antihermitian matrix test.\end{DoxyVerb}
 \\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}
\begin{DoxyAuthor}{Author}
L. M. Thompson 
\end{DoxyAuthor}
\begin{DoxyDate}{Date}
2017 
\end{DoxyDate}

\index{mqc\_matrix\_vector\_at@{mqc\_matrix\_vector\_at}!mqc\_algebra@{mqc\_algebra}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{mqc\_matrix\_vector\_at()}{mqc\_matrix\_vector\_at()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily type(\mbox{\hyperlink{structmqc__algebra_1_1mqc__vector}{mqc\+\_\+vector}}) function mqc\+\_\+algebra\+::mqc\+\_\+matrix\+\_\+vector\+\_\+at (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{class(\mbox{\hyperlink{structmqc__algebra_1_1mqc__matrix}{mqc\+\_\+matrix}}), intent(in)}]{Mat,  }\item[{integer(kind=int64), dimension(\+:), intent(in)}]{Rows,  }\item[{integer(kind=int64), dimension(\+:), intent(in)}]{Cols }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}



{\bfseries{ M\+Q\+C\+\_\+\+Matrix\+\_\+\+Vector\+\_\+\+At is a function that returns the subvector of an ~\newline
 M\+QC matrix}} 

\begin{DoxyParagraph}{Purpose\+:}
\begin{DoxyVerb}    MQC_Matrix_Vector_At is a function that returns the subvector of an MQC matrix.
    The row and column specification are given as a vector where one vector must 
    contain a single non-zero integer to specify the row or column of the 
    subvector, and the other vector must be either zero or two non-zero integers to
    specify the range of elements that will form the subvector. If the value of an
    element specification is negative, it counts from the last element back. If the
    value of an element specification is zero, the whole row/column is specified.\end{DoxyVerb}
 
\end{DoxyParagraph}

\begin{DoxyParams}[1]{Parameters}
\mbox{\texttt{ in}}  & {\em Mat} & \begin{DoxyVerb}        Mat is Class(MQC_Matrix)
        The MQC matrix from which to return the subvector.\end{DoxyVerb}
\\
\hline
\mbox{\texttt{ in}}  & {\em Rows} & \begin{DoxyVerb}        Rows is Integer(kind=int64),Dimension(:)
        The specification of the rows to include in the 
        subvector. 
        If = [A,B]: output is subvector of rows A to B
          If (A,B)>0 row count is from first index
          If (A,B)<0 row count is from last index
        If = [0]: subvector of rows equivalent to [1,-1].\end{DoxyVerb}
\\
\hline
\mbox{\texttt{ in}}  & {\em Cols} & ~\newline
 \begin{DoxyVerb}        Cols is Integer(kind=int64),Dimension(:)
        The specification of the columns to include in the 
        subvector. 
        If = [A,B]: output is subvector of columns A to B
          If (A,B)>0 column count is from first index
          If (A,B)<0 column count is from last index
        If = [0]: subvector of columns equivalent to [1,-1].\end{DoxyVerb}
 \\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}
\begin{DoxyAuthor}{Author}
L. M. Thompson 
\end{DoxyAuthor}
\begin{DoxyDate}{Date}
2017 
\end{DoxyDate}

{\bfseries{ M\+Q\+C\+\_\+\+Matrix\+\_\+\+Vector\+\_\+\+Put is a subroutine that writes a subvector to the specified position of a M\+QC matrix}} 

\begin{DoxyParagraph}{Purpose\+:}
\begin{DoxyVerb}    MQC_Matrix_Vector_Put is a subroutine that writes a subvector to the specified
    position of a MQC matrix. The row and column specification are given as a vector 
    where one vector must contain a single non-zero integer to specify the row or 
    column where the subvector will be written, and the other vector must be either 
    zero or two non-zero integers to specify the range of elements that will be
    overwritten by the subvector. If the value of an element specification is 
    negative, it counts from the last element back. If the value of an element 
    specification is zero, the whole row/column is specified.\end{DoxyVerb}
 
\end{DoxyParagraph}

\begin{DoxyParams}[1]{Parameters}
\mbox{\texttt{ in,out}}  & {\em Mat} & \begin{DoxyVerb}        Mat is Class(MQC_Matrix)
        The MQC matrix from which to return the subvector.\end{DoxyVerb}
\\
\hline
\mbox{\texttt{ in}}  & {\em Vector\+In} & \begin{DoxyVerb}        VectorIn is Type(MQC_Vector)
        The subvector to overwrite at the specified elements 
        of Mat.\end{DoxyVerb}
\\
\hline
\mbox{\texttt{ in}}  & {\em Rows} & \begin{DoxyVerb}        Rows is Integer(kind=int64),Dimension(:)
        The specification of the rows to include in the 
        subvector. 
        If = [A,B]: output is subvector of rows A to B
          If (A,B)>0 row count is from first index
          If (A,B)<0 row count is from last index
        If = [0]: subvector of rows equivalent to [1,-1].\end{DoxyVerb}
\\
\hline
\mbox{\texttt{ in}}  & {\em Cols} & ~\newline
 \begin{DoxyVerb}        Cols is Integer(kind=int64),Dimension(:)
        The specification of the columns to include in the 
        subvector. 
        If = [A,B]: output is subvector of columns A to B
          If (A,B)>0 column count is from first index
          If (A,B)<0 column count is from last index
        If = [0]: subvector of columns equivalent to [1,-1].\end{DoxyVerb}
 \\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}

{\bfseries{ M\+Q\+C\+\_\+\+R4\+Tensor\+\_\+\+At is a function that returns the value of an ~\newline
 element of a M\+QC rank-\/4 tensor}} 

\begin{DoxyParagraph}{Purpose\+:}
\begin{DoxyVerb}    MQC_R4Tensor_At is a function that returns the value of (I,J,K,L)th element of 
    a MQC rank-4 tensor as an MQC scalar. If I, J, K or L is negative, the (N-I+1)th 
    index is selected.\end{DoxyVerb}
 
\end{DoxyParagraph}

\\
\hline

 \begin{DoxyVerb}        I is Integer(kind=int64)
        The first dimension of the element in MQC rank-4 tensor
          If I>0 row count is from first index
          If I<0 row count is from last index.\end{DoxyVerb}
\\
\hline
\mbox{\texttt{ in}}  & {\em J} & ~\newline
 \begin{DoxyVerb}        J is Integer(kind=int64)
        The second dimension of the element in MQC rank-4 tensor
          If J>0 row count is from first index
          If J<0 row count is from last index.\end{DoxyVerb}
\\
\hline
\mbox{\texttt{ in}}  & {\em K} & ~\newline
 \begin{DoxyVerb}        K is Integer(kind=int64)
        The third dimension of the element in MQC rank-4 tensor
          If K>0 row count is from first index
          If K<0 row count is from last index.\end{DoxyVerb}
\\
\hline
\mbox{\texttt{ in}}  & {\em L} & ~\newline
 \begin{DoxyVerb}        L is Integer(kind=int64)
        The fourth dimension of the element in MQC rank-4 tensor
          If L>0 row count is from first index
          If L<0 row count is from last index.\end{DoxyVerb}
 \\

{\bfseries{ M\+Q\+C\+\_\+\+R4\+Tensor\+\_\+\+Put is a subroutine that updates the value of an ~\newline
 element of a M\+QC rank-\/4 tensor}} 

\begin{DoxyParagraph}{Purpose\+:}
\begin{DoxyVerb}    MQC_R4Tensor_Put is a subroutine that updates the value of (I,J,K,L)th element 
    of a MQC rank-4 tensor. If I, J, K or L is negative, the (N-I+1)th index is 
    selected.\end{DoxyVerb}

          If I<0 row count is from last index.\end{DoxyVerb}

{\footnotesize\ttfamily logical function mqc\+\_\+algebra\+::mqc\+\_\+realgtscalar (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{interfacemqc__algebra_1_1real}{real}}(kind=real64), intent(in)}]{Real\+In,  }\item[{type(\mbox{\hyperlink{structmqc__algebra_1_1mqc__scalar}{mqc\+\_\+scalar}}), intent(in)}]{Scalar }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}



{\bfseries{ M\+Q\+C\+\_\+\+Real\+G\+T\+Scalar is a function that returns T\+R\+UE if an intrinsic real is greater than a M\+Q\+C\+\_\+\+Scalar}} 

\begin{DoxyParagraph}{Purpose\+:}
\begin{DoxyVerb}    MQC_RealGTScalar is a function that returns TRUE if an intrinsic real is greater 
    than a MQC_Scalar. 

    When dealing with complex numbers, the function returns TRUE if the intrinsic real
    is greater than the real part of the MQC_Scalar and FALSE if the intrinsic real is 
    less than the real part of the MQC_Scalar. If the intrinsic real is equal to the
    real part of the MQC_Scalar, the function returns TRUE if the imaginary part of 
    MQC_Scalar is less than zero and FALSE otherwise.\end{DoxyVerb}
 
\end{DoxyParagraph}

\begin{DoxyParams}[1]{Parameters}
\mbox{\texttt{ in}}  & {\em Real\+In} & \begin{DoxyVerb}        RealIn is Real(kind=real64)
        The intrinsic real that will be tested.\end{DoxyVerb}
\\
\hline
\mbox{\texttt{ in}}  & {\em Scalar} & \begin{DoxyVerb}        Scalar is Type(MQC_Scalar)
        The MQC_Scalar that will be tested.\end{DoxyVerb}
 \\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}

L. M. Thompson

\index{mqc\_algebra@{mqc\_algebra}!mqc\_scalar\_get\_random\_value@{mqc\_scalar\_get\_random\_value}}
\index{mqc\_scalar\_get\_random\_value@{mqc\_scalar\_get\_random\_value}!mqc\_algebra@{mqc\_algebra}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{mqc\_scalar\_get\_random\_value()}{mqc\_scalar\_get\_random\_value()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily subroutine mqc\+\_\+algebra\+::mqc\+\_\+scalar\+\_\+get\+\_\+random\+\_\+value (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{class(\mbox{\hyperlink{structmqc__algebra_1_1mqc__scalar}{mqc\+\_\+scalar}})}]{Scalar,  }\item[{integer, dimension(\+:), optional}]{Seed,  }\item[{character(len=$\ast$), intent(in), optional}]{Distribution }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}



{\bfseries{ M\+Q\+C\+\_\+\+Scalar\+\_\+\+Get\+\_\+\+Random\+\_\+\+Value is a function that returns a random real value from a specified distribution}} 

\begin{DoxyParagraph}{Purpose\+:}
\begin{DoxyVerb}    MQC_Scalar_Get_Random_Value is a function that returns a random real 
    value from an optionally specified distribution. Note that the range of
    values varies by distribution. In addition, a seed can be specified for 
    consistent greneration of the same number. Default options are uniform 
    distribution with random seed. The following options are available:
    
    1. Distribution = 'uniform' uses a uniform distribution between 0 and 1. 
    2. Distribution = 'gaussian' uses a normal distribution with zero mean and
                      unit variance obtained using the Box-Muller transformation
    3. Distribution = 'exp' uses an exponential distribution (lambda=1.0) 
                      returning positive integers. 
    4. Distribution = 'exp01' uses an exponential distribution (lambda=8.0)that 
                      gives values in the range 0 and 1. \end{DoxyVerb}
 
\end{DoxyParagraph}

\begin{DoxyParams}[1]{Parameters}
\mbox{\texttt{ in,out}}  & {\em Scalar} & \begin{DoxyVerb}        Scalar is Class(MQC_Scalar)
        The MQC_Scalar to be filled. \end{DoxyVerb}
\\
\hline
\mbox{\texttt{ in}}  & {\em Seed} & \begin{DoxyVerb}        Seed is integer,dimension(:),optional 
        Integer array containing seed. Note in gfortran
        only the first two elements affect the value of
        the random number.\end{DoxyVerb}
\\
\hline
\mbox{\texttt{ in}}  & {\em Distribution} & \begin{DoxyVerb}        Distribution is character(len=*),intent(in),optional 
        Distribution of the function from which random number
        is selected.
        = 'uniform':  uniform between 0 and 1
        = 'gaussian': normal deviation with zero mean and unit 
                      variance
        = 'exp':      exponential decay y=\exp(-x)
        = 'exp01':    exponential decay between 0 and 1 obtained
                      using mod(y,1.0) of y=\exp(-8x).\end{DoxyVerb}
 \\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}
\begin{DoxyAuthor}{Author}
X. Dong ~\newline
 

L. M. Thompson ~\newline
 
\end{DoxyAuthor}
\begin{DoxyDate}{Date}
2019 
\end{DoxyDate}

{\footnotesize\ttfamily logical function mqc\+\_\+algebra\+::mqc\+\_\+scalarge (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{type(\mbox{\hyperlink{structmqc__algebra_1_1mqc__scalar}{mqc\+\_\+scalar}}), intent(in)}]{Scalar1,  }\item[{type(\mbox{\hyperlink{structmqc__algebra_1_1mqc__scalar}{mqc\+\_\+scalar}}), intent(in)}]{Scalar2 }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}



{\bfseries{ M\+Q\+C\+\_\+\+Scalar\+GE is a function that returns T\+R\+UE if the left M\+Q\+C\+\_\+\+Scalar is greater than or equal the right M\+Q\+C\+\_\+\+Scalar}} 

\begin{DoxyParagraph}{Purpose\+:}
\begin{DoxyVerb}    MQC_ScalarGE is a function that returns TRUE if the left MQC_Scalar is greater than or
    equal to the right MQC_Scalar. 

    When dealing with complex numbers, the function returns TRUE if the left real part is
    is greater than or equal to the right real part and FALSE if the left real part is less
    than the right real part.\end{DoxyVerb}
 
\end{DoxyParagraph}

\begin{DoxyParams}[1]{Parameters}

{\footnotesize\ttfamily logical function mqc\+\_\+algebra\+::mqc\+\_\+scalargt (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{type(\mbox{\hyperlink{structmqc__algebra_1_1mqc__scalar}{mqc\+\_\+scalar}}), intent(in)}]{Scalar1,  }\item[{type(\mbox{\hyperlink{structmqc__algebra_1_1mqc__scalar}{mqc\+\_\+scalar}}), intent(in)}]{Scalar2 }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}



{\bfseries{ M\+Q\+C\+\_\+\+Scalar\+GT is a function that returns T\+R\+UE if the left M\+Q\+C\+\_\+\+Scalar is greater than the right M\+Q\+C\+\_\+\+Scalar}} 

\begin{DoxyParagraph}{Purpose\+:}
\begin{DoxyVerb}    MQC_ScalarGT is a function that returns TRUE if the left MQC_Scalar is greater than
    the right MQC_Scalar. 

    When dealing with complex numbers, the function returns TRUE if the left real part 
    is greater than the right real part and FALSE if the left real part is less than 
    the right real part. If the left real part is equal to the right real part, the 
    function returns TRUE if the left imaginary part is greater than the right imaginary 
    part and FALSE otherwise.\end{DoxyVerb}
 
\end{DoxyParagraph}

\begin{DoxyParams}[1]{Parameters}
\mbox{\texttt{ in}}  & {\em Scalar1} & \begin{DoxyVerb}        Scalar1 is Type(MQC_Scalar)
        The first MQC_Scalar that will be tested.\end{DoxyVerb}
\\
\hline
\mbox{\texttt{ in}}  & {\em Scalar2} & \begin{DoxyVerb}        Scalar2 is Type(MQC_Scalar)
        The second MQC_Scalar that will be tested.\end{DoxyVerb}
 \\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}

{\bfseries{ M\+Q\+C\+\_\+\+Scalar\+G\+T\+Integer is a function that returns T\+R\+UE if a M\+Q\+C\+\_\+\+Scalar is greater than an intrinsic integer}} 

\begin{DoxyParagraph}{Purpose\+:}
\begin{DoxyVerb}    MQC_ScalarGTInteger is a function that returns TRUE if a MQC_Scalar is greater than an 
    intrinsic integer.

    When dealing with complex numbers, the function returns TRUE if the real part of the 
    MQC_Scalar is greater than the intrinsic integer and FALSE if the real part of the 
    MQC_Scalar is less than the intrinsic integer. If the real part of the MQC_Scalar is 
    equal to the intrinsic integer, the function returns TRUE if the imaginary part of 
    MQC_Scalar is greater than zero and FALSE otherwise.\end{DoxyVerb}
 
\end{DoxyParagraph}

{\footnotesize\ttfamily logical function mqc\+\_\+algebra\+::mqc\+\_\+scalarltreal (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{type(\mbox{\hyperlink{structmqc__algebra_1_1mqc__scalar}{mqc\+\_\+scalar}}), intent(in)}]{Scalar,  }\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{interfacemqc__algebra_1_1real}{real}}(kind=real64), intent(in)}]{Real\+In }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}



{\bfseries{ M\+Q\+C\+\_\+\+Scalar\+L\+T\+Real is a function that returns T\+R\+UE if a M\+Q\+C\+\_\+\+Scalar is less than an intrinsic real}} 

\begin{DoxyParagraph}{Purpose\+:}
\begin{DoxyVerb}    MQC_ScalarLTReal is a function that returns TRUE if a MQC_Scalar is less than an 
    intrinsic real.

    When dealing with complex numbers, the function returns TRUE if the real part of the 
    MQC_Scalar is less than the intrinsic real and FALSE if the real part of the MQC_Scalar
    is greater than the intrinsic real. If the real part of the MQC_Scalar is equal to the
    intrinsic real, the function returns TRUE if the imaginary part of MQC_Scalar is less 
    than zero and FALSE otherwise. \end{DoxyVerb}
 
\end{DoxyParagraph}

\begin{DoxyParams}[1]{Parameters}
\mbox{\texttt{ in}}  & {\em Scalar} & \begin{DoxyVerb}        Scalar is Type(MQC_Scalar)
        The MQC_Scalar that will be tested.\end{DoxyVerb}
\\
\hline
\mbox{\texttt{ in}}  & {\em Real\+In} & \begin{DoxyVerb}        RealIn is Real(kind=real64)
        The intrinsic real that will be tested.\end{DoxyVerb}
 \\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}

L. M. Thompson 
\end{DoxyAuthor}
\begin{DoxyDate}{Date}
2019 
\end{DoxyDate}

\index{mqc\_algebra@{mqc\_algebra}!mqc\_vector\_norm@{mqc\_vector\_norm}}
\index{mqc\_vector\_norm@{mqc\_vector\_norm}!mqc\_algebra@{mqc\_algebra}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{mqc\_vector\_norm()}{mqc\_vector\_norm()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily type(\mbox{\hyperlink{structmqc__algebra_1_1mqc__scalar}{mqc\+\_\+scalar}}) function mqc\+\_\+algebra\+::mqc\+\_\+vector\+\_\+norm (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{class(\mbox{\hyperlink{structmqc__algebra_1_1mqc__vector}{mqc\+\_\+vector}}), intent(inout)}]{vector,  }\item[{character(len=1), intent(in), optional}]{method\+In }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}



{\bfseries{ M\+Q\+C\+\_\+\+Vector\+\_\+\+Norm is a function that returns the norm of an M\+QC vector}} 

\begin{DoxyParagraph}{Purpose\+:}
\begin{DoxyVerb}    MQC_Vector_Norm is a function that returns the norm of an MQC vector. The 
    following options are available:

    1. methodIn = 'M' uses the maximum absolute value max(abs(A(i))).
    2. methodIn = '1' uses the one norm.
    3. methodIn = 'I' uses the infinity norm.
    4. methodIn = 'F' uses the Frobenius norm (default).\end{DoxyVerb}
 
\end{DoxyParagraph}

\begin{DoxyParams}[1]{Parameters}
\mbox{\texttt{ in,out}}  & {\em Vector} & \begin{DoxyVerb}        Vector is Class(MQC_Vector)
        The name of the MQC_Vector variable.\end{DoxyVerb}
\\
\hline
\mbox{\texttt{ in}}  & {\em Method\+In} & \begin{DoxyVerb}        MethodIn is Character(len=1)
        = 'M': max(abs(A(i)))
        = '1': one norm
        = 'I': infinity norm
        = 'F': Frobenius norm.\end{DoxyVerb}

{\bfseries{ Sym\+Index\+Hash is a function that returns the index in a vector of a symmetric-\/packed matrix or rank-\/4 tensor}} 

\begin{DoxyParagraph}{Purpose\+:}
\begin{DoxyVerb}    SymIndexHash is a function that returns the index in a vector of a symmetric-
    packed matrix or rank-4 tensor. If a matrix is tested, it is assumed lower-
    triangular row-wise stored.\end{DoxyVerb}
 
\end{DoxyParagraph}

\begin{DoxyParams}[1]{Parameters}
\mbox{\texttt{ in}}  & {\em I} & \begin{DoxyVerb}        I is integer(kind=int64)
        The first index of the matrix/rank-4 tensor.\end{DoxyVerb}
\\
\hline
\mbox{\texttt{ in}}  & {\em J} & \begin{DoxyVerb}        I is integer(kind=int64)
        The second index of the matrix/rank-4 tensor.\end{DoxyVerb}
\\
\hline
\mbox{\texttt{ in}}  & {\em K} & \begin{DoxyVerb}        K is integer(kind=int64),Optional
        The third index of the rank-4 tensor. This argument is
        only required when taking hash of a rank-4 tensor.\end{DoxyVerb}
\\
\hline
\mbox{\texttt{ in}}  & {\em L} & \begin{DoxyVerb}        L is integer(kind=int64),Optional
        The fourth index of the rank-4 tensor. This argument is
        only required when taking hash of a rank-4 tensor.\end{DoxyVerb}
 \\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}
